colspan="2">\n</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; background:#C0D077;"><center>Last completed</center></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<i><a href="/wiki/2018_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2018 Wimbledon Championships">2018 Wimbledon</a></i></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>The Championships, Wimbledon</b>, commonly known simply as <b>Wimbledon</b>, is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> <a href="/wiki/Tournament" title="Tournament">tournament</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It has been held at the <a href="/wiki/All_England_Lawn_Tennis_and_Croquet_Club" title="All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club">All England Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon,_London" title="Wimbledon, London">Wimbledon</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, since 1877 and is played on outdoor <a href="/wiki/Grass_court" title="Grass court">grass courts</a>.\n</p><p>Wimbledon is one of the four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tennis tournaments, the others being the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">French Open</a> and the <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>. Since the Australian Open shifted to <a href="/wiki/Hardcourt" title="Hardcourt">hardcourt</a> in 1988, Wimbledon is the only major still played on <a href="/wiki/Grass_court" title="Grass court">grass</a>.\n</p><p>The tournament traditionally took place over two weeks in late June and early July, starting on the last Monday in June and culminating with the Ladies\' and Gentlemen\'s Singles Finals, scheduled for the Saturday and Sunday at the end of the second week. However recent changes to the tennis calendar have seen the event moved back by a week to begin in early July.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Five major events are held each year, with additional junior and invitational competitions also taking place.\n</p><p>Wimbledon traditions include a strict dress code for competitors and Royal patronage. <a href="/wiki/Strawberry#Uses" title="Strawberry">Strawberries and cream</a> is traditionally consumed at the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, fans consumed 34,000 kg of English strawberries and 10,000 litres of cream.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The tournament is also notable for the absence of sponsor advertising around the courts. In 2009, Wimbledon\'s <a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a> was fitted with a <a href="/wiki/Retractable_roof" title="Retractable roof">retractable roof</a> to lessen the loss of playing time due to rain.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spencer_gore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Spencer_gore.jpg/170px-Spencer_gore.jpg" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Spencer_gore.jpg/255px-Spencer_gore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Spencer_gore.jpg/340px-Spencer_gore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="345" data-file-height="496" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spencer_gore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Spencer_Gore_(sportsman)" title="Spencer Gore (sportsman)">Spencer Gore</a>, the winner of the <a href="/wiki/1877_Wimbledon_Championship" title="1877 Wimbledon Championship">inaugural Wimbledon Championship</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning">Beginning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/All_England_Lawn_Tennis_and_Croquet_Club" title="All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club">All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club</a> is a private club founded on 23 July 1868, originally as "The All England Croquet Club". Its first ground was at Nursery Road off Worple Road, Wimbledon.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1876, <a href="/wiki/Lawn_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawn tennis">lawn tennis</a>, a game devised by Major <a href="/wiki/Walter_Clopton_Wingfield" title="Walter Clopton Wingfield">Walter Clopton Wingfield</a> a year or so earlier as an outdoor version of <a href="/wiki/Court_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Court tennis">court tennis</a> and originally given the name <i>Sphairistik\xc3\xa8</i>, was added to the activities of the club. In spring 1877, the club was renamed "The All England Croquet and Lawn Tennis Club" and signalled its change of name by instituting the first Lawn Tennis Championship. A new code of laws, replacing the code administered by the <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a>, was drawn up for the event. Today\'s rules are similar except for details such as the height of the net and posts and the distance of the service line from the net.\n</p><p>The inaugural <a href="/wiki/1877_Wimbledon_Championship" title="1877 Wimbledon Championship">1877 Wimbledon Championship</a> started on 9 July 1877 and the Gentlemen\'s Singles was the only event held. It was won by <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Gore_(sportsman)" title="Spencer Gore (sportsman)">Spencer Gore</a>, an old Harrovian <a href="/wiki/Rackets_(sport)" title="Rackets (sport)">rackets</a> player, from a field of 22. About 200 spectators paid one shilling each to watch the final.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lawns at the ground were arranged so that the principal court was in the middle with the others arranged around it, hence the title "<a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-centrecourt_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-centrecourt-16">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> The name was retained when the Club moved in 1922 to the present site in Church Road, although no longer a true description of its location.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However, in 1980 four new courts were brought into commission on the north side of the ground, which meant the Centre Court was once more correctly described. The opening of the new No. 1 Court in 1997 emphasised the description.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg/220px-1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg/330px-1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg/440px-1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1349" data-file-height="973" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1884_wimbledon_ladies_program.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ladies <a href="/wiki/1884_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1884 Wimbledon Championships">Championship, 1884</a>. First prize, awarded to <a href="/wiki/Maud_Watson" title="Maud Watson">Maud Watson</a>, was a silver flower-basket worth 20 <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(British_coin)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinea (British coin)">guineas</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>By 1882, activity at the club was almost exclusively confined to lawn tennis and that year the word "croquet" was dropped from the title. However, for sentimental reasons it was restored in 1899.\n</p><p>In 1884, the club added <a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_ladies%27_singles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon ladies&#39; singles champions">Ladies\' Singles</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_gentlemen%27s_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon gentlemen&#39;s doubles champions">Gentlemen\'s Doubles</a> competitions. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_ladies%27_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon ladies&#39; doubles champions">Ladies\' Doubles</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_mixed_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon mixed doubles champions">Mixed Doubles</a> events were added in 1913. Until 1922, the reigning champion had to play only in the final, against whomever had won through to challenge him/her. As with the other three <i>Major or Grand Slam</i> events, Wimbledon was contested by top-ranked amateur players, professional players were prohibited from participating. This changed with the advent of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_tennis" title="History of tennis">open era</a> in 1968. No British man won the singles event at Wimbledon between <a href="/wiki/Fred_Perry" title="Fred Perry">Fred Perry</a> in 1936 and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a> in 2013, while no British woman has won since <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Wade" title="Virginia Wade">Virginia Wade</a> in 1977, although <a href="/wiki/Annabel_Croft" title="Annabel Croft">Annabel Croft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laura_Robson" title="Laura Robson">Laura Robson</a> won the Girls\' Championship in <a href="/wiki/1984_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1984 Wimbledon Championships">1984</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2008 Wimbledon Championships">2008</a> respectively. The Championship was first televised in 1937.\n</p><p>Though properly called "The Championships, Wimbledon", depending on sources the event is also known as "The All England Lawn Tennis Championships", "The Wimbledon Championships" or simply "Wimbledon". From 1912 to 1924, the tournament was recognized by the <a href="/wiki/International_Lawn_Tennis_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Lawn Tennis Federation">International Lawn Tennis Federation</a> as the "World Grass Court Championships".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Wimbledon is considered the world\'s premier tennis tournament and the priority of the Club is to maintain its leadership. To that end a long-term plan was unveiled in 1993, intended to improve the quality of the event for spectators, players, officials and neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Stage one (1994\xe2\x80\x931997) of the plan was completed for the 1997 championships and involved building the new No. 1 Court in Aorangi Park, a broadcast centre, two extra grass courts and a tunnel under the hill linking Church Road and Somerset Road. Stage two (1997\xe2\x80\x932009) involved the removal of the old No. 1 Court complex to make way for the new Millennium Building, providing extensive facilities for players, press, officials and members, and the extension of the West Stand of the Centre Court with 728 extra seats. Stage three (2000\xe2\x80\x932011) has been completed with the construction of an entrance building, club staff housing, museum, bank and ticket office.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new retractable roof was built in time for the 2009 championships, marking the first time that rain did not stop play for a lengthy time on <a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a>. The Club tested the new roof at an event called <i>A Centre Court Celebration</i> on Sunday, 17 May 2009, which featured exhibition matches involving <a href="/wiki/Andre_Agassi" title="Andre Agassi">Andre Agassi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steffi_Graf" title="Steffi Graf">Steffi Graf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Clijsters" title="Kim Clijsters">Kim Clijsters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Henman" title="Tim Henman">Tim Henman</a>. The first Championship match to take place under the roof was the completion of the fourth round women\'s singles match between <a href="/wiki/Dinara_Safina" title="Dinara Safina">Dinara Safina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9lie_Mauresmo" title="Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo">Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo</a>.  The first match to be played in its entirety under the new roof took place between <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanislas_Wawrinka" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanislas Wawrinka">Stanislas Wawrinka</a> on 29 June 2009. Murray was also involved in the match completed latest in the day at Wimbledon, which ended at 11:02&#160;pm in a victory over <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Baghdatis" title="Marcos Baghdatis">Marcos Baghdatis</a> at Centre Court in the third round of the 2012 Championships. The 2012 Men\'s Singles Final on 8 July 2012, between <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> and Murray, was the first singles final to be partially played under the roof, which was activated during the third set.<sup id="cite_ref-monday_final_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-monday_final-20">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new 4000-seat <a href="/wiki/No._2_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="No. 2 Court">No. 2 Court</a> was built on the site of the old No. 13 Court in time for the 2009 Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  A new 2000-seat <a href="/wiki/No._3_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 3 Court (Wimbledon)">No. 3 Court</a> was built on the site of the old No. 2 and No. 3 Courts.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Wimbledon consists of five main events, four junior events and seven invitation events.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_events">Main events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Main events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Court_roof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Centre_Court_roof.jpg/220px-Centre_Court_roof.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Centre_Court_roof.jpg/330px-Centre_Court_roof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Centre_Court_roof.jpg/440px-Centre_Court_roof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Court_roof.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a> with open roof at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2010 Wimbledon Championships">2010 Championships</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The five main events, and the number of players (or teams, in the case of doubles) are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Gentlemen\'s Singles (128)</li>\n<li>Ladies\' Singles (128)</li>\n<li>Gentlemen\'s Doubles (64)</li>\n<li>Ladies\' Doubles (64)</li>\n<li>Mixed Doubles (48)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_events">Junior events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Junior events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The four junior events and the number of players or teams are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Boys\' Singles (64)</li>\n<li>Girls\' Singles (64)</li>\n<li>Boys\' Doubles (32)</li>\n<li>Girls\' Doubles (32)</li></ul>\n<p>No mixed doubles event is held at this level.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invitation_events">Invitation events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Invitation events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The seven invitational events and the number of pairs are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Gentlemen\'s Invitation Doubles (8 pairs Round Robin)<sup id="cite_ref-gentlemen_invitation_doubles_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gentlemen_invitation_doubles-24">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Ladies\' Invitation Doubles (8 pairs Round Robin)</li>\n<li>Senior Gentlemen\'s Invitation Doubles (8 pairs Round Robin)<sup id="cite_ref-senior_gentlemen_invitation_doubles_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senior_gentlemen_invitation_doubles-25">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Gentlemen\'s Wheelchair Singles<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Ladies\' Wheelchair Singles</li>\n<li>Gentlemen\'s Wheelchair Doubles (4 pairs)<sup id="cite_ref-Wheelchair_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wheelchair-27">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Ladies\' Wheelchair Doubles (4 pairs)<sup id="cite_ref-Wheelchair_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wheelchair-27">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_formats">Match formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Match formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Matches in the Gentlemen\'s Singles and Gentlemen\'s Doubles are best-of-five sets; all other events are best-of-three sets.  A tiebreak game is played if the score reaches 6\xe2\x80\x936 in any set except the fifth (in a five-set match) or the third (in a three-set match), in which case a two-game lead must be reached.\n</p><p>All events are <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">single-elimination tournaments</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-single_elimination_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-single_elimination-28">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> except for the Gentlemen\'s, Senior Gentlemen\'s and the Ladies\' Invitation Doubles, which are <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin tournaments</a>.\n</p><p>Until 1922, the winners of the previous year\'s competition (except in the Ladies\' Doubles and Mixed Doubles) were automatically granted <a href="/wiki/Bye_(sports)" title="Bye (sports)">byes</a> into the final round (then known as the challenge round). This led to many winners retaining their titles in successive years, as they were able to rest while their opponent competed from the start of the competition. From 1922, the prior year\'s champions were required to play all the rounds, like other tournament competitors.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Schedule">Schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Each year the tournament began on the last Monday in June, two weeks after the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Club_Championships" title="Queen&#39;s Club Championships">Queen\'s Club Championships</a>, which is one of the men\'s major warm-up tournaments, together with the <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Weber_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerry Weber Open">Gerry Weber Open</a>, which is held in <a href="/wiki/Halle,_North_Rhine-Westphalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Halle, North Rhine-Westphalia">Halle, Germany</a>, during the same week. It was announced that the <a href="/wiki/2017_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2017 Wimbledon Championships">2017 tournament</a> would begin on Monday 3 July.<sup id="cite_ref-dates_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dates-29">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Other grass-court tournaments before Wimbledon are <a href="/wiki/Eastbourne_International" title="Eastbourne International">Eastbourne</a>, England, and <a href="/wiki/Rosmalen_Grass_Court_Championships" title="Rosmalen Grass Court Championships">Rosmalen</a> in the Netherlands, both combining mixed events. The other women\'s warm-up tournament for Wimbledon is <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Classic_(tennis)" title="Birmingham Classic (tennis)">Birmingham</a>, also in England. The only grass-court tournament scheduled after the Championships is the <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame_Tennis_Championships" title="Hall of Fame Tennis Championships">Hall of Fame Tennis Championships</a> at <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a>, USA, which takes place the week after Wimbledon.\n</p><p>Wimbledon is scheduled for 14 days, beginning on a Monday and ending on a Sunday. Before 1982 it ended a day earlier, with the women\'s singles final on the Friday and the men\'s singles final on the Saturday.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The five main events span both weeks, but the junior and invitational events are held mainly during the second week.  Traditionally, unlike the other three tennis Grand Slams, there is no play on the "Middle Sunday", which is considered a rest day.  However, rain has forced play on the Middle Sunday four times, in 1991, 1997, 2004 and 2016. On the first of these four occasions, Wimbledon staged a "People\'s Sunday", with unreserved seating and readily available, inexpensive tickets, allowing those with more limited means to sit on the show courts.\n</p><p>The second Monday at Wimbledon is often called "Manic Monday", because it is the busiest day with the last-16 matches for both men\'s and women\'s singles, where fans have a pick of watching on a single day, any of the best 32 players left; which is also unique in a Grand Slam singles competition.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2015, the championships have begun one week later than in previous years, extending the gap between the tournament and the <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">French Open</a> from two to three weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Additionally the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Open" title="Stuttgart Open">Stuttgart Open</a> men\'s tournament converted to a grass surface and was rescheduled from July to June, extending the grass court season.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players_and_seeding">Players and seeding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Players and seeding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Both the men\'s and ladies\' singles consist of 128 players.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Players and doubles pairs are admitted to the main events on the basis of their international rankings, with 104 direct entries into the men\'s and 108 into the ladies\' competitions. Both tournaments have 8 <a href="/wiki/Wild_card_(sports)#Professional_tennis" title="Wild card (sports)">wild card</a> entrants, with the remainder in each made up of qualifiers. Since the 2001 tournament, 32 players have been given <a href="/wiki/Seed_(sports)" title="Seed (sports)">seedings</a> in the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' singles, 16 teams in the doubles events. The system of seeding was introduced during the <a href="/wiki/1924_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1924 Wimbledon Championships">1924 Wimbledon Championships</a>. This was a simplified version allowing countries to nominate four players who were placed in different quarters of the draw. This system was replaced for the <a href="/wiki/1927_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1927 Wimbledon Championships">1927 Wimbledon Championships</a> and from then on players were seeded on merit. The first players to be seeded as no. 1 were <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Lacoste" title="Ren\xc3\xa9 Lacoste">Ren\xc3\xa9 Lacoste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helen_Wills" title="Helen Wills">Helen Wills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-compendium2013_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compendium2013-34">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Committee of Management decide which players receive wildcards. Usually, wild cards are players who have performed well during previous tournaments or would stimulate public interest in Wimbledon by participating. The only wild card to win the Gentlemen\'s Singles Championship was <a href="/wiki/Goran_Ivani%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Goran Ivani\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87">Goran Ivani\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87</a> in 2001. Players and pairs who neither have high enough rankings nor receive wild cards may participate in a qualifying tournament held one week before Wimbledon at the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> Sports Ground in <a href="/wiki/Roehampton" title="Roehampton">Roehampton</a>. The singles qualifying competitions are three-round events; the same-sex doubles competitions last for only one round. There is no qualifying tournament for Mixed Doubles. The furthest that any qualifier has progressed in a Singles tournament is the semi-final round: <a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a> in 1977 (Gentlemen\'s Singles), <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Voltchkov" title="Vladimir Voltchkov">Vladimir Voltchkov</a> in 2000 (Gentlemen\'s Singles), and <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Stevenson" title="Alexandra Stevenson">Alexandra Stevenson</a> in 1999 (Ladies\' Singles).\n</p><p>Players are admitted to the junior tournaments upon the recommendations of their national tennis associations, on their <a href="/wiki/International_Tennis_Federation" title="International Tennis Federation">International Tennis Federation</a> world rankings and, in the case of the singles events, on the basis of a qualifying competition. The Committee of Management determines which players may enter the four invitational events.\n</p><p>The Committee seeds the top players and pairs on the basis of their rankings, but it can change the seedings based on a player\'s previous grass court performance. Since 2002 a seeding committee has not been required for the Gentlemen\'s Singles following an agreement with the ATP. While the seeds are still the top 32 players according to rankings, the seeding order is determined using the formula: ATP Entry System Position points + 100% points earned for all grass court tournaments in the past 12 months + 75% points earned for the best grass court tournament in the 12 months before that.<sup id="cite_ref-seedingexplained_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seedingexplained-35">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> A majority of the entrants are unseeded. Only two unseeded players have won the Gentlemen\'s Singles: <a href="/wiki/Boris_Becker" title="Boris Becker">Boris Becker</a> in 1985 and <a href="/wiki/Goran_Ivani%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Goran Ivani\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87">Goran Ivani\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87</a> in 2001. In 1985 there were only 16 seeds and Becker was ranked 20th; Ivani\xc5\xa1evi\xc4\x87 was ranked 125th when he won as a Wild Card entrant, although he had previously been a finalist three times, and been ranked no. 2 in the world; his low ranking was due to having been hampered by a persistent shoulder injury for three years, which had only just cleared up. In 1996, the title was won by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Krajicek" title="Richard Krajicek">Richard Krajicek</a>, who was originally unseeded (ranked 17th, and only 16 players were seeded) but was promoted to a seeded position (still with the number 17) when Thomas Muster withdrew before the tournament. No unseeded player has captured the Ladies\' Singles title; the lowest seeded female champion was <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a>, who won in 2007 as the 23rd seed; Williams was returning from an injury that had prevented her playing in previous tournaments, giving her a lower ranking than she would normally have had. Unseeded pairs have won the doubles titles on numerous occasions; the 2005 Gentlemen\'s Doubles champions were not only unseeded, but also (for the first time ever) qualifiers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grounds">Grounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg/220px-Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg/330px-Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg/440px-Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cmglee_London_Wimbledon_Championships_venue_aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the grounds</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/All_England_Lawn_Tennis_and_Croquet_Club" title="All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club">All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club</a></div>\n<p>Since 2001, the courts used for Wimbledon have been sown with 100% <a href="/wiki/Ryegrass" class="mw-redirect" title="Ryegrass">perennial ryegrass</a>. Prior to 2001 a combination of 70% ryegrass and 30% <a href="/wiki/Creeping_Red_Fescue" class="mw-redirect" title="Creeping Red Fescue">Creeping Red Fescue</a> was used. The change was made to improve durability and strengthen the sward to better withstand the increasing wear of the modern game.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main show courts, <a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a> and <a href="/wiki/No._1_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 1 Court (Wimbledon)">No. 1 Court</a>, are normally used for only two weeks a year, during the Championships, but play can extend into a third week in exceptional circumstances. The remaining 17 courts are regularly used for other events hosted by the Club. The show courts were in action for the second time in three months in 2012 as Wimbledon hosted the tennis events of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Games</a>. One of the show courts is also used for home ties of the GB teams in the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> on occasions.\n</p><p>Wimbledon is the only Grand Slam event played on grass courts. At one time, all the Majors, except the French Open, were played on grass. The <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a> abandoned grass in 1975 and the Australian Open in 1988.\n</p><p>The principal court, <a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a>, was opened in 1922 when the Club moved from Worple Road to Church Road. The Church Road venue was larger and was needed to meet the ever-growing public demand.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg/220px-Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg/330px-Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg/440px-Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_order_of_play.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The order of play for all courts is displayed on boards around the grounds</div></div></div>\n<p>Due to the possibility of rain during Wimbledon, a retractable roof was installed prior to the 2009 Championship. It is designed to close/open in about 20 minutes and will be closed primarily to protect play from inclement (and, if necessary, extremely hot) weather during The Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> When the roof is being opened or closed, play is suspended. The first time the roof was closed during a Wimbledon Championship match was on Monday 29 June 2009, involving <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9lie_Mauresmo" title="Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo">Am\xc3\xa9lie Mauresmo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dinara_Safina" title="Dinara Safina">Dinara Safina</a>. The first full match played and completed under the roof featured <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stan_Wawrinka" title="Stan Wawrinka">Stan Wawrinka</a>, played on the same date. \n</p><p>The court has a capacity of 15,000. At its south end is the Royal Box, from which members of the Royal Family and other dignitaries watch matches. Centre Court usually hosts the finals and semifinals of the main events, as well as many matches in the earlier rounds involving top-seeded players or local favourites.\n</p><p>The second most important court is <a href="/wiki/No._1_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 1 Court (Wimbledon)">No. 1 Court</a>. The court was constructed in 1997 to replace the old No.1 Court, which was adjacent to Centre Court.  The old No.1 Court was demolished because its capacity for spectators was too low. The court was said to have had a unique, more intimate atmosphere and was a favourite of many players. The new No.1 Court has a capacity of approximately 11,000. Construction on a new retractable roof on the No.1 Court began after the 2017 Championships and is set to be completed in 2019. The capacity of the stadium is also set to rise by 900 taking the total capacity up to 12,400.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2009, a new <a href="/wiki/No._2_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 2 Court (Wimbledon)">No. 2 Court</a> is being used at Wimbledon with a capacity for 4,000 people. To obtain <a href="/wiki/Planning_permission" title="Planning permission">planning permission</a>, the playing surface is around 3.5m below ground level, ensuring that the single-storey structure is only about 3.5m above ground level, and thus not affecting local views.<sup id="cite_ref-Wim_18_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wim_18-40">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Plans to build on the current site of Court 13 were dismissed due to the high capacity of games played at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Games</a>. The old No.2 Court has been renamed as <a href="/wiki/No._3_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 3 Court (Wimbledon)">No.3 Court</a>. The old No.2 Court was known as the "Graveyard of Champions" because many highly seeded players were eliminated there during early rounds over the years, including <a href="/wiki/Ilie_N%C4%83stase" title="Ilie N\xc4\x83stase">Ilie N\xc4\x83stase</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Becker" title="Boris Becker">Boris Becker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Agassi" title="Andre Agassi">Andre Agassi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martina_Hingis" title="Martina Hingis">Martina Hingis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sharapova" title="Maria Sharapova">Maria Sharapova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The court has a capacity of 2,192 + 770 standing. In 2011 a new No.3 Court and a new Court 4 were unveiled on the sites of the old No.2 and 3 courts.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG/220px-Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG/330px-Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG/440px-Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_court_No._1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View from seats of Wimbledon Court No. 1</div></div></div>\n<p>Because of the summer climate in southern England, Wimbledon employs \'Court Attendants\' each year, who work to maintain court conditions. Their principal responsibility is to ensure that the courts are quickly covered when it begins to rain, so that play can resume as quickly as possible once the referees decide to uncover the courts. The court attendants are mainly university students working to make summer money. Centre Court is covered by full-time groundstaff, however.\n</p><p>At the northern end of the grounds is a giant television screen on which important matches are broadcast. Fans watch from an area of grass officially known as the <a href="/wiki/Aorangi_Terrace" class="mw-redirect" title="Aorangi Terrace">Aorangi Terrace</a>. When British players do well at Wimbledon, the hill attracts fans for them, and is often renamed after them by the press: <a href="/wiki/Greg_Rusedski" title="Greg Rusedski">Greg Rusedski</a>\'s followers convened at "Rusedski Ridge", and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Henman" title="Tim Henman">Tim Henman</a> has had the hill nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Henman_Hill" title="Henman Hill">Henman Hill</a>. As both of them have now retired and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a> is the number 1 British player, the hill is occasionally referred to as "Murray Mound" or "<a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">Murrayfield</a>", as a reference to his Scottish heritage and the Scottish rugby ground of the same name, but this has largely failed to catch on \xe2\x80\x93 the area is still usually referred to as Henman Hill. None of these nicknames are official.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bank_of_England_Sports_Centre">Bank of England Sports Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bank of England Sports Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The qualifying matches, prior to the main draw, take place at the Bank of England Sports Ground, in <a href="/wiki/Roehampton" title="Roehampton">Roehampton</a>, 3.6 miles (5.8&#160;km) from the All-England Club.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG/220px-Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG/330px-Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG/440px-Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Court_10_2004_RJL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Court 10 \xe2\x80\x93 on the outside courts there is no reserved seating</div></div></div>\n<p>Social commentator Ellis Cashmore describes Wimbledon as having "a <a href="/wiki/David_Niven" title="David Niven">David Niven</a>-ish propriety", conforming to the standards of behaviour common in the 1950s. Writer <a href="/wiki/Peter_York" title="Peter York">Peter York</a> sees the event as representing a particular white and affluent type of Britishness, describing the area of Wimbledon as "a southern, well off, late-Victorian suburb with a particular social character". Cashmore has criticised the event for being "remote and insulated" from the changing multicultural character of modern Britain, describing it as "nobody\'s idea of all-things-British".<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-44">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ball_boys_and_ball_girls">Ball boys and ball girls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ball boys and ball girls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the championship games, <a href="/wiki/Ball_boy" title="Ball boy">ball boys</a> and girls, known as BBGs, play a crucial role in the smooth running of the tournament, with a brief that a good BBG "should not be seen. They should blend into the background and get on with their jobs quietly."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1947 ball boys were supplied by Goldings,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> the only <a href="/wiki/Barnardos" class="mw-redirect" title="Barnardos">Barnardos</a> school to provide them. Prior to this, from the 1920s onwards, the ball boys had been provided by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Ashley-Cooper,_7th_Earl_of_Shaftesbury" title="Anthony Ashley-Cooper, 7th Earl of Shaftesbury">The Shaftesbury Children\'s Home</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg/220px-Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg/330px-Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg/440px-Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_ballgirl_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wimbledon ball girl at the net, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1969, BBGs have been provided by local schools. As of 2008 they are drawn from schools in the London boroughs of <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Merton" title="London Borough of Merton">Merton</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Sutton" title="London Borough of Sutton">Sutton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Borough_of_Kingston_upon_Thames" title="Royal Borough of Kingston upon Thames">Kingston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Wandsworth" title="London Borough of Wandsworth">Wandsworth</a>, as well as from <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally, Wandsworth Boys Grammar School in Sutherland Grove, Southfields and Mayfield Girls School on <a href="/wiki/West_Hill,_Wandsworth" title="West Hill, Wandsworth">West Hill</a> in Wandsworth, both now defunct, were the schools of choice for selection of BBGs. This was possibly owing to their proximity to the club. BBGs have an average age of 15, being drawn from the school years <a href="/wiki/Year_Nine" title="Year Nine">nine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Year_Ten" title="Year Ten">ten</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Site_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Site-48">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> BBGs will serve for one, or if re-selected, up to five tournaments, from Year Nine to Year Thirteen.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Starting in 2005, BBGs work in teams of six, two at the net, four at the corners, and teams rotate one hour on court, one hour off, (two hours depending on the court) for the day\'s play.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Site_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Site-48">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Teams are not told which court they will be working on the day, to ensure the same standards across all courts. With the expansion of the number of courts, and lengthening the tennis day, as of 2008, the number of BBGs required is around 250. From the second Wednesday, BBGs are told to leave the Championships, leaving around 80 on the final Sunday. Each BBG receives a certificate, a can of used balls, a group photograph and a programme when leaving. BBG service is paid, with a total of \xc2\xa3120-\xc2\xa3180 being paid to each ball boy\nor girl after the 13-day period depending on the number of days served. Every BBG keeps all of their kit, typically consisting of three or four shirts, two or three shorts or <a href="/wiki/Skorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Skorts">skorts</a>, track suit bottoms and top, twelve pairs of socks, three pairs of wristbands, a hat, water bottle holder, bag and trainers. Along with this it is seen as a privilege, and seen as a valuable addition to a school leaver\'s <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_vitae" title="Curriculum vitae">curriculum vitae</a>, showing discipline. BBG places are split 50:50 between boys and girls, with girls having been used since 1977, appearing on centre court since 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prospective BBGs are first nominated by their school <a href="/wiki/Headteacher" class="mw-redirect" title="Headteacher">headteacher</a>, to be considered for selection. To be selected, a candidate must pass written tests on the rules of tennis, and pass fitness, mobility and other suitability tests, against initial preliminary instruction material. Successful candidates then commence a training phase, starting in February, in which the final BBGs are chosen through continual assessment. As of 2008, this training intake was 600. The training includes weekly sessions of physical, procedural and theoretical instruction, to ensure that the BBGs are fast, alert, self-confident and adaptable to situations. As of 2011, early training occurs at the Wimbledon All England Lawn Tennis Club Covered Courts, to the side of the Grounds, and then moves to outside courts (8, 9, 10) the week before the Championships for a feel of the grass court.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours_and_uniforms">Colours and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Colours and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG/220px-Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG/330px-Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG/440px-Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Grojean_2004_RJL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Grosjean" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Grosjean">S\xc3\xa9bastien Grosjean</a> takes a shot on Court 18 during the <a href="/wiki/2004_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2004 Wimbledon Championships">2004 Championships</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Dark green and purple are the traditional Wimbledon colours. However, all tennis players participating in the tournament are required to wear all-white or at least almost all-white clothing, a long-time tradition at Wimbledon.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clothing_guidelines_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clothing_guidelines-53">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> Wearing white clothing with some colour accents is also acceptable, provided the colour scheme is not that of an identifiable commercial brand logo (the outfitter\'s brand logo being the sole exception). Controversy followed <a href="/wiki/Martina_Navratilova" title="Martina Navratilova">Martina Navratilova</a>\'s wearing branding for "Kim" cigarettes in 1982. Green clothing was worn by the chair umpire, linesmen, ball boys and ball girls until the 2005 Championships; however, beginning with the 2006 Championships, officials, ball boys and ball girls were dressed in new navy blue- and cream-coloured uniforms from American designer <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Lauren" title="Ralph Lauren">Ralph Lauren</a>. This marked the first time in the history of the Championships that an outside company was used to design Wimbledon clothing; the contract with <a href="/wiki/Polo_Ralph_Lauren" class="mw-redirect" title="Polo Ralph Lauren">Polo Ralph Lauren</a> ended in 2015.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Referring_to_players">Referring to players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Referring to players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By tradition, the "Men\'s" and "Women\'s" competitions are referred to as "Gentlemen\'s" and "Ladies\'" competitions at Wimbledon. The junior competitions are referred to as the "Boys\'" and "Girls\'" competitions.\n</p><p>Prior to 2009 female players were referred to by the title "Miss" or "Mrs" on scoreboards. As dictated by strict rule of etiquette, married female players are referred to by their husbands\' names: for example, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evert" title="Chris Evert">Chris Evert</a> appeared on scoreboards as "Mrs. J. M. Lloyd" during her marriage to <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_(tennis)" title="John Lloyd (tennis)">John Lloyd</a>, since <a href="/wiki/Coverture#Outside_the_legal_realm" title="Coverture">"Mrs. X" essentially designates the wife of X</a>. This tradition has continued at least to some extent.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> For the first time during the 2009 tournament, players were referred to on scoreboards by both their first and last names.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The title "Mr" is not used for male players who are professionals on scoreboards but the prefix is retained for amateurs, although chair umpires refer to players as "Mr" when they use the replay challenge. The chair umpire will say "Mr &lt;surname&gt; is challenging the call..." and "Mr &lt;surname&gt; has X challenges remaining."   However, the umpires still say Miss/Missus &lt;surname&gt; when announcing the score of the Ladies\' matches.\n</p><p>If a match is being played with two competitors of the same surname (e.g. Venus and Serena Williams, Bob and Mike Bryan), the chair umpire will specify to whom they are referring by stating the player\'s first name and surname during announcements (e.g. "Game, Miss Venus Williams", "Advantage, Mike Bryan").\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_family">Royal family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Royal family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court,_Wimbledon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg/220px-The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg/330px-The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg/440px-The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court%2C_Wimbledon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Gallery_at_Centre_Court,_Wimbledon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Royal Gallery at Centre Court, Wimbledon</div></div></div>\n<p>Previously, players bowed or curtsied to members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Family">royal family</a> seated in the Royal Box upon entering or leaving Centre Court. However, in 2003, All England Club president <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince Edward, Duke of Kent">Prince Edward, Duke of Kent</a> decided to discontinue the tradition. Now, players are required to bow or curtsy only if The <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">The Queen</a> is present,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> as was in practice during the 2010 Championships when the Queen was in attendance at Wimbledon on 24 June.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 27 June 2012, Roger Federer said in his post-match interview that he and his opponent had been asked to bow towards the Royal Box as Prince Charles and his wife were present, saying that it wasn\'t a problem for him.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_stewards">Services stewards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Services stewards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Prior to the Second World War, members of the <a href="/wiki/Brigade_of_Guards" title="Brigade of Guards">Brigade of Guards</a> and retired members of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Artillery" title="Royal Artillery">Royal Artillery</a> performed the role of stewards. In 1946 the AELTC offered employment to wartime servicemen returning to civilian life during their demobilisation leave. Initially, this scheme extended only to the Royal Navy, followed by the Army in 1947 and the Royal Air Force in 1949. In 1965 London Fire Brigade members joined the ranks of stewards.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The service stewards, wearing uniform, are present in Centre Court and No.\'s 1, 2, 3, 12 and 18 courts.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, 595 Service and London Fire Brigade stewards attended.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Only enlisted members of the Armed Forces may apply for the role, which must be taken as leave, and half of each year\'s recruits must have stewarded at Wimbledon before. The AELTC pays a subsistence allowance to servicemen and women working as stewards to defray their accommodation costs for the period of the Championships. The Service Stewards are not to be confused with the 185 Honorary Stewards.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tickets">Tickets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tickets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg/220px-WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg/330px-WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg/440px-WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="966" data-file-height="724" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WimbledonResaleTicket2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wimbledon operates a ticket resale system where returned Show Court tickets can be purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> All proceeds go to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png/220px-Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png/330px-Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png/440px-Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="292" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon2016QueueCard.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queue cards are presented to those queuing for admission to Wimbledon.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This helps to prevent queue jumping.</div></div></div>\n<p>The majority of centre and show court tickets sold to the general public have since 1924 been made available by a public ballot that the All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club holds at the start of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The ballot has always been substantially oversubscribed. Successful applicants are selected at random by a computer.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The most recent figures from 2011 suggested there were four applicants to every ballot ticket. Applications must be posted to arrive at the AELTC by the last day of December in the year prior to the tournament. Seats and days are allocated randomly and ballot tickets are not transferrable.\n</p><p>The All England Club, through its subsidiary The All England Lawn Tennis Ground plc, issues <a href="/wiki/Debentures" class="mw-redirect" title="Debentures">Debentures</a> to tennis fans every five years to raise funds for capital expenditure. Fans who invest thus in the club receive a pair of tickets for every day of the Wimbledon Championships for the five years the investment lasts.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Only debenture holders are permitted to sell on their tickets to third parties and demand for debentures has increased in recent years, to such an extent that they are even traded on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>.\n</p><p>Wimbledon and the French Open are the only Grand Slam tournaments where fans without tickets for play can queue up and still get seats on the three show courts on the day of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  Sequentially numbered queue cards were introduced in 2003. From 2008, there is a single queue, allotted about 500 seats for each court. When they join the queue, fans are handed queue cards. Anyone who then wishes to leave the queue temporarily, even if in possession of a queue card, must agree their position with the others nearby in the queue and/or a steward.\n</p><p>To get access to the show courts, fans will normally have to queue overnight.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> This is done by fans from all over the world and, although considered vagrancy, is part of the Wimbledon experience in itself. The All-England Club allows overnight queuing and provides toilet and water facilities for campers. Early in the morning when the line moves towards the Grounds, stewards walk along the line and hand out wristbands that are colour-coded to the specific court. The wrist band (and payment) is exchanged at the ticket office for the ticket when the grounds open. General admission to the grounds gives access to the outer courts and is possible without queuing overnight. Tickets returned by people leaving early go on sale at 2:30&#160;pm and the money goes to charity. Queuing for the show courts ends after the quarter finals have been completed.\n</p><p>At 2.40pm on Day Seven (Monday 28 June) of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2010 Wimbledon Championships">2010 Championships</a>, the one-millionth numbered Wimbledon queue card was handed out to Rose Stanley from South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Wimbledon is notable for the longest running sponsorship in sports history due to its association with <a href="/wiki/Slazenger" title="Slazenger">Slazenger</a> who have supplied all tennis balls during the tournament since 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Since 1935 Wimbledon has a sponsorship association with the <a href="/wiki/Robinsons_(drink)" title="Robinsons (drink)">Robinsons</a> fruit drink brand.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_Wimbledon">Radio Wimbledon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Radio Wimbledon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Radio_Wimbledon" title="Radio Wimbledon">Radio Wimbledon</a></div>\n<p>Until 2011 when its contract ended, <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Radio Wimbledon could be heard within a five-mile radius on 87.7 <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a>, and also online. It operated under a <a href="/wiki/Restricted_Service_Licence" title="Restricted Service Licence">Restricted Service Licence</a>. Presenters included Sam Lloyd and Ali Barton. Typically they worked alternate four-hour shifts until the end of the last match of the day. Reporters and commentators included Gigi Salmon, Nick Lestor, Rupert Bell, Nigel Bidmead, Guy Swindells, Lucie Ahl, Nadine Towell and Helen Whitaker. Often they reported from the "Crow\'s Nest", an elevated building housing the Court 3 and 4 scoreboards which affords views of most of the outside courts. Regular guests included Sue Mappin. In later years Radio Wimbledon acquired a second low-power FM frequency (within the grounds only) of 96.3 FM for uninterrupted Centre Court commentary, and, from 2006, a third for coverage from No. 1 Court on 97.8 FM. Hourly news bulletins and travel (using <a href="/wiki/Radio_Data_System" title="Radio Data System">RDS</a>) were also broadcast.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_coverage">Television coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Television coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Beginning with the <a href="/wiki/2018_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2018 Wimbledon Championships">2018 tournament</a>, an in-house operation known as Wimbledon Broadcasting Services (WBS) has served as the official host broadcaster of the tournament, replacing <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg/220px-Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg/330px-Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg/440px-Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3862" data-file-height="2172" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_Championships_Canary_Wharf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People watching the Championships\' broadcast in <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1937 the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has broadcast the tournament on television in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbccoverage_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbccoverage-78">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> The matches covered are primarily split between its two main terrestrial channels, <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a>, and their Red Button service. This can result in live matches being moved across all 3 channels. The BBC holds the broadcast rights for Wimbledon until 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>  During the days of <a href="/wiki/British_Satellite_Broadcasting" title="British Satellite Broadcasting">British Satellite Broadcasting</a>, its sports channel carried extra coverage of Wimbledon for subscribers. One of the most notable British commentators was <a href="/wiki/Dan_Maskell" title="Dan Maskell">Dan Maskell</a>, who was known as the BBC\'s "voice of tennis" until his retirement in 1991. <a href="/wiki/John_Barrett_(tennis)" title="John Barrett (tennis)">John Barrett</a> succeeded him in that role until he retired in 2006. Current commentators working for the BBC at Wimbledon include British ex-players <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Castle" title="Andrew Castle">Andrew Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_(tennis)" title="John Lloyd (tennis)">John Lloyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Henman" title="Tim Henman">Tim Henman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Rusedski" title="Greg Rusedski">Greg Rusedski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Smith_(tennis)" title="Samantha Smith (tennis)">Samantha Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Petchey" title="Mark Petchey">Mark Petchey</a>; tennis legends such as <a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Austin" title="Tracy Austin">Tracy Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Becker" title="Boris Becker">Boris Becker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Davenport" title="Lindsay Davenport">Lindsay Davenport</a>; and general sports commentators including <a href="/wiki/David_Mercer_(broadcaster)" title="David Mercer (broadcaster)">David Mercer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Davies" title="Barry Davies">Barry Davies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cotter" title="Andrew Cotter">Andrew Cotter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mullins" title="Nick Mullins">Nick Mullins</a>. The coverage is presented by <a href="/wiki/Sue_Barker" title="Sue Barker">Sue Barker</a> (live) and <a href="/wiki/Claire_Balding" class="mw-redirect" title="Claire Balding">Claire Balding</a> (highlights). Previous BBC presenters include <a href="/wiki/Des_Lynam" title="Des Lynam">Des Lynam</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Vine" title="David Vine">David Vine</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Inverdale" title="John Inverdale">John Inverdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Carpenter" title="Harry Carpenter">Harry Carpenter</a>.\n</p><p>The Wimbledon Finals are obliged to be shown live and in full on terrestrial television (BBC Television Service, ITV, Channel 4, or Channel 5) by government mandate. Highlights of the rest of the tournament must be provided by terrestrial stations; live coverage (excepting the finals) may be sought by satellite or cable TV.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The BBC was forced to apologise after many viewers complained about "over-talking" by its commentary team during the TV coverage of the event in 2011. It said in a statement that views on commentary were subjective but that they "do appreciate that over-talking can irritate our audience". The BBC added that it hoped it had achieved "the right balance" across its coverage and was "of course sorry if on occasion you have not been satisfied". <a href="/wiki/Tim_Henman" title="Tim Henman">Tim Henman</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a> were among the ex-players commentating.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Wimbledon was also involved in a piece of television history, when on 1 July 1967 the first official <a href="/wiki/Colour_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Colour television">colour television</a> broadcast took place in the UK. Four hours live coverage of the <a href="/wiki/1967_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1967 Wimbledon Championships">1967 Championships</a> was shown on BBC Two, which was the first television channel in Europe to regularly broadcast in colour. Footage of that historic match no longer survives, however, the Gentlemen\'s Final of that year is still held in the BBC archives because it was the first Gentlemen\'s Final transmitted in colour. Since 2007, Wimbledon matches have been transmitted in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high-definition</a>, originally on the BBC\'s free-to-air channel <a href="/wiki/BBC_HD" title="BBC HD">BBC HD</a>, with continual live coverage during the tournament of Centre Court and Court No. 1 as well as an evening highlights show <i><a href="/wiki/Today_at_Wimbledon" title="Today at Wimbledon">Today at Wimbledon</a></i>.  Coverage is now shown on BBC One and Two\'s HD feeds. Beginning 2018, all centre court matches are televised in <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K</a> <a href="/wiki/Ultra-high-definition_television" title="Ultra-high-definition television">ultra-high-definition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The BBC\'s opening theme music for Wimbledon was composed by <a href="/wiki/Keith_Mansfield" title="Keith Mansfield">Keith Mansfield</a> and is titled "Light and Tuneful". A piece titled "A Sporting Occasion" is the traditional closing theme, though nowadays coverage typically ends either with a montage set to a popular song or with no music at all. Mansfield also composed the piece "World Champion", used by NBC during intervals (change-overs, set breaks, etc.) and at the close of broadcasts throughout the tournament.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann">RT\xc3\x89</a> broadcast the tournament during the 1980s and 1990s on their second channel <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Two">RT\xc3\x89 Two</a>, they also provided highlights of the games in the evening. The commentary provided was given by Matt Doyle a former Irish-American professional tennis player and Jim Sherwin a former RT\xc3\x89 newsreader. Caroline Murphy was the presenter of the programme. RT\xc3\x89 made the decision in 1998 to discontinue broadcasting the tournament due to falling viewing figures and the large number of viewers watching on the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> From 2005 until 2014 <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a> Ireland\'s Irish-language broadcaster provided coverage of the tournament.
