Live coverage was provided in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> while they broadcast highlights in English at night.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 Wimbledon moved to pay TV broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Setanta_Sports" title="Setanta Sports">Setanta Sports</a> under a 3-year agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Its successor, <a href="/wiki/Eir_Sport" title="Eir Sport">Eir Sport</a>, currently hosts broadcasting rights in Ireland.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the United States, <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> began showing taped highlights of the Wimbledon Gentlemen\'s Singles Final in the 1960s on its <i><a href="/wiki/Wide_World_of_Sports_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Wide World of Sports (U.S. TV series)">Wide World of Sports</a></i> series. <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> began covering Wimbledon in 1969, with same-day taped (and often edited) coverage of the Gentlemen\'s Singles Final. In 1979, the network began carrying the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' Singles Finals live. For the next few decades, Americans made a tradition of <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>\'s "Breakfast at Wimbledon"<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> specials at weekends. Live coverage started early in the morning (the US being a minimum of 5 hours behind the UK) and continued well into the afternoon, interspersed with commentary and interviews from <a href="/wiki/Bud_Collins" title="Bud Collins">Bud Collins</a>, whose tennis acumen and (in)famous patterned trousers were well known to tennis fans in the US. Collins was sacked by <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> in 2007, but was promptly hired by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, the cable home for The Championships in the States. For many years NBC\'s primary Wimbledon host was veteran broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Dick_Enberg" title="Dick Enberg">Dick Enberg</a>.\n</p><p>From 1975 to 1999, premium channel <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> carried weekday coverage of Wimbledon. Hosts included <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lampley" title="Jim Lampley">Jim Lampley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billie_Jean_King" title="Billie Jean King">Billie Jean King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martina_Navratilova" title="Martina Navratilova">Martina Navratilova</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Lloyd_(tennis)" title="John Lloyd (tennis)">John Lloyd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barry_MacKay" title="Barry MacKay">Barry MacKay</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously, weekday coverage in the United States was exclusively handled by <a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">ESPN2</a> during the tournament\'s first week.  During the tournament\'s second week it was split between ESPN2 and NBC.  ESPN\'s online service <a href="/wiki/ESPN3" title="ESPN3">ESPN3</a> provides full coverage of courts not televised using BBC graphics and commentary. Since the 2012 tournament, all live coverage, including the Finals, has been exclusively on ESPN and ESPN2, marking the second major tennis championship (after the Australian Open) available in the United States exclusively on pay television (although taped highlights from the tournament are presented at weekend afternoons on sister network <a href="/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC" title="ESPN on ABC">ABC</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Taped coverage using the world feed is aired in primetime and overnights on <a href="/wiki/Tennis_Channel" title="Tennis Channel">Tennis Channel</a> and is branded <i>Wimbledon Primetime</i>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, coverage of Wimbledon is exclusively carried by <a href="/wiki/The_Sports_Network" title="The Sports Network">TSN</a> and <a href="/wiki/RDS_Info" title="RDS Info">RDS</a>, which are co-owned by Bell Media and ESPN.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a> family of networks has aired Wimbledon since the early 1960s.  Presently, most weekend matches are broadcast through <a href="/wiki/Canal_5_(Televisa_Network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal 5 (Televisa Network)">Canal 5</a> with the weekday matches broadcast on the <a href="/wiki/Televisa_Deportes_Network" title="Televisa Deportes Network">Televisa Deportes Network</a>.  As Mexico is six hours behind the U.K., some Canal 5 affiliates air the weekend matches as the first program of the day after <a href="/wiki/Sign-on" class="mw-redirect" title="Sign-on">sign-on</a>.  Although Mexico had begun broadcasting in colour in 1962, Wimbledon continued to air in black and white in Mexico until colour television came to the United Kingdom in 1967.\n</p><p>In most of the remainder of Latin America, Wimbledon airs on <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN Latin America">ESPN</a>, as do the other Grand Slam tournaments. In Brazil, <a href="/wiki/SporTV" title="SporTV">SporTV</a> has exclusive rights to the broadcast.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_countries">Other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In several European countries, Wimbledon is shown live on <a href="/wiki/Eurosport_1" title="Eurosport 1">Eurosport 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurosport_2" title="Eurosport 2">Eurosport 2</a> and the Eurosport Player. Although there are some exceptions, as in Denmark, where the Danish channel <a href="/wiki/TV3_Sport" title="TV3 Sport">TV3 Sport</a> and Viaplay, holds the rights to show Wimbledon until 2019. In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> Center Court is shown live on <a href="/wiki/Eurosport_1" title="Eurosport 1">Eurosport 1</a> and all other courts are shown live on the Eurosport Player. But Court One is covered live on <a href="/wiki/Ziggo_Sport" title="Ziggo Sport">Ziggo Sport</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ziggo_Sport_Select" class="mw-redirect" title="Ziggo Sport Select">Ziggo Sport Select</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the free-to-air <a href="/wiki/Nine_Network" title="Nine Network">Nine Network</a> covered Wimbledon for almost 40 years but decided to drop their broadcast following the 2010 tournament, citing declining ratings and desire to use money saved to bid on other sports coverage. In April 2011, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a>, the host broadcaster of the Australian Open, along with its sister channel <a href="/wiki/7Two" class="mw-redirect" title="7Two">7Two</a> would broadcast the event from 2011. Pay television network <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(Australia)" title="Fox Sports (Australia)">Fox Sports Australia</a> also covers the event. In <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and its Subcontinental region, it is broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Star_Sports" title="Star Sports">Star Sports</a>.\n</p><p>Coverage is free-to-air in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> through <a href="/wiki/TVNZ_One" class="mw-redirect" title="TVNZ One">TVNZ One</a>, beginning each night at 11 pm (midday in London).  In 2017 their new channel, <a href="/wiki/TVNZ_Duke" title="TVNZ Duke">TVNZ Duke</a> (also free-to-air), carried an alternative to the main feed, including (for example) matches on outside courts involving New Zealand players.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Asia" title="Fox Sports Asia">Fox Sports Asia</a> holds broadcasting rights across Southeast Asia.\n</p><p>Most matches are also available for viewing through internet betting websites and other live streaming services, as television cameras are set up to provide continuous coverage on nearly all the courts.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophies_and_prize_money">Trophies and prize money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Trophies and prize money">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophies">Trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_trophies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wimbledon_trophies.jpg/220px-Wimbledon_trophies.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wimbledon_trophies.jpg/330px-Wimbledon_trophies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wimbledon_trophies.jpg/440px-Wimbledon_trophies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1706" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wimbledon_trophies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ladies\' (top) and Gentlemen\'s singles trophies</div></div></div>\n<p>The Gentlemen\'s Singles champion is presented with a silver gilt cup 18.5&#160;inches (about 47&#160;cm) in height and 7.5&#160;inches (about 19&#160;cm) in diameter. The trophy has been awarded since 1887 and bears the inscription: "All England Lawn Tennis Club Single Handed Championship of the World". The actual trophy remains the property of the All England Club in their museum, so the champion receives a three-quarter size replica of the Cup bearing the names of all past Champions (height 13.5 inches, 34cm).<sup id="cite_ref-wimbledon_trophies_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimbledon_trophies-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ladies\' Singles champion is presented with a sterling silver salver commonly known as the "<a href="/wiki/Venus_Rosewater_Dish" title="Venus Rosewater Dish">Venus Rosewater Dish</a>", or simply the "Rosewater Dish". The salver, which is 18.75&#160;inches (about 48&#160;cm) in diameter, is decorated with figures from mythology.  The actual dish remains the property of the All England Club in their museum, so the champion receives a miniature replica bearing the names of all past Champions. From 1949 to 2006 the replica was 8 inches in diameter, and since 2007 it has been a three-quarter size replica with a diameter of 13.5 inches.<sup id="cite_ref-wimbledon_trophies_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimbledon_trophies-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The winner of the Gentlemen\'s Doubles, Ladies\' Doubles, and Mixed Doubles events receive silver cups. A trophy is awarded to each player in the Doubles pair, unlike the other <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournaments where the winning Doubles duo shares a single trophy. The Gentlemen\'s Doubles silver challenge cup was originally from the Oxford University Lawn Tennis Club and donated to the All England Club in 1884. The Ladies\' Doubles Trophy, a silver cup and cover known as The Duchess of Kent Challenge Cup, was presented to the All England Club in 1949 by The Duchess of Kent. The Mixed Doubles Trophy is a silver challenge cup and cover presented to the All England Club by the family of two-time Wimbledon doubles winner S.H. Smith.<sup id="cite_ref-wimbledon_trophies_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimbledon_trophies-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg/220px-Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg" width="220" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg/330px-Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg/440px-Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="1368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodbridge_Wimbledon_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Todd_Woodbridge" title="Todd Woodbridge">Todd Woodbridge</a> holding the Gentlemen\'s Doubles silver challenge cup in 2004</div></div></div>\n<p>The runner-up in each event receives an inscribed silver plate. The trophies are usually presented by the President of the All England Club, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince Edward, Duke of Kent">The Duke of Kent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wimbledon_trophies_89-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimbledon_trophies-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_money">Prize money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Prize money">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Prize money was first awarded in <a href="/wiki/1968_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1968 Wimbledon Championships">1968</a>, the year that professional players were allowed to compete in the Championships for the first time. Total prize money was \xc2\xa326,150; the winner of the men\'s title earned \xc2\xa32,000 while the women\'s singles champion received \xc2\xa3750.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before 2007, among grand slam tournaments, Wimbledon and the French Open awarded more prize money in men\'s events than in women\'s events. In 2007, Wimbledon changed this policy, awarding the same amounts per event category to both men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The decision has been controversial because women generally spend considerably less time playing on court than men (except in mixed doubles) owing to their wins being based upon best of three sets, whereas men\'s are based upon best of five sets.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, a total of \xc2\xa312,500,000 in prize money was awarded with the singles champions receiving \xc2\xa3850,000 each, an increase of 13.3 percent on 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 total prize money increased to \xc2\xa313,725,000, and the singles champions received \xc2\xa31,000,000 each. A further increase of 6.4% in 2011 resulted in a total prize money amount of \xc2\xa314,600,000. Both male and female singles champions prize money increased to \xc2\xa31,100,000, a rise of 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The 2012 Championships offered total prize money of \xc2\xa316,060,000, an increase of 10.0% from 2011. The bulk of the increases were given to players losing in earlier rounds.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> This move was in response to the growing angst among lower-ranked players concerning the inadequacy of their pay. <a href="/wiki/Sergiy_Stakhovsky" title="Sergiy Stakhovsky">Sergiy Stakhovsky</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals#Structure" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">ATP Player Council</a> and who was at the time ranked 68th, was among the most vocal in the push for higher pay for players who bow out in the earlier rounds. In an interview Stakhovsky intimated that it is not uncommon for lower-ranked players to be in the negative, for certain tour events, if their results weren\'t stellar.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  This issue gained the attention of the men\'s "<a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(tennis)" title="Big Four (tennis)">Big Four</a>"\xe2\x80\x94Novak Djokovic, Roger Federer, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a>, and Rafael Nadal\xe2\x80\x94as well as the Championships.\n</p><p>In 2013 total prize money was further increased by about 40% from 2012 to \xc2\xa322,560,000. The losers in the earlier singles rounds of the tournament saw a highest 62% increase in their pay while the total prize money of the doubles increased by 22%. The prize money for participants of the qualifying matches saw an increase of 41%. <a href="/wiki/Sergiy_Stakhovsky" title="Sergiy Stakhovsky">Sergiy Stakhovsky</a>, a member of the  <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals#Structure" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">ATP Player Council</a>, was the loudest voice for this increase.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The 2015 prize money was \xc2\xa31,880,000 each for the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' Singles winners, \xc2\xa3340,000 each pair for the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' Doubles winners, and \xc2\xa3100,000 per pair for the Mixed Doubles winners. The total prize money awarded is \xc2\xa326,750,000 up 7% from the \xc2\xa325,000,000 in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-prizemoney2016_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prizemoney2016-102">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2016_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2016 Wimbledon Championships">2016 Wimbledon Championships</a> saw prize money for the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' Singles winners reach \xc2\xa32,000,000 for the first time. The winning pair of the Gentlemen\'s and Ladies\' Doubles received \xc2\xa3350,000, a \xc2\xa310,000 increase from 2015. \xc2\xa3100,000 was awarded to the winning pair of the Mixed Doubles competition.\n</p><p>In 2016, the total prize money of \xc2\xa328,100,000 was a 5% increase on the 2015 prize money.\n</p><p>In 2017, the total prize money rose by 12.5% to \xc2\xa331,600,000, with the Gentlemen\xe2\x80\x99s and Ladies\xe2\x80\x99 Singles Champions each receiving \xc2\xa32.2 million, a 10% increase from \xc2\xa32.0 million in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-prize-money-2017_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prize-money-2017-103">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n<caption>2017 Gentlemen\'s &amp; Ladies\' Singles Prize Money<sup id="cite_ref-prize-money-2017_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prize-money-2017-103">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Category\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Amount each\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Increase from 2016\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Winners\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa32,200,000</td>\n<td>10.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Runners-up\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa31,100,000</td>\n<td>10.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Losing semifinalists\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa3550,000</td>\n<td>10.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Losing quarterfinalists\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa3275,000</td>\n<td>10.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Fourth round losers\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa3147,000</td>\n<td>11.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Third round losers\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa390,000</td>\n<td>12.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Second round losers\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa357,000</td>\n<td>14.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">First round losers\n</th>\n<td>\xc2\xa335,000</td>\n<td>16.7%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_points">Ranking points</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ranking points">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Ranking points for the <a href="/wiki/ATP_Rankings" title="ATP Rankings">ATP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women&#39;s Tennis Association">WTA</a> have varied at Wimbledon through the years but at present singles players receive the following points:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center; width: 20em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">\n</th>\n<th scope="col">ATP\n</th>\n<th scope="col">WTA\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">First round\n</th>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>10\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Second round\n</th>\n<td>45</td>\n<td>70\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Third round\n</th>\n<td>90</td>\n<td>130\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Fourth round\n</th>\n<td>180</td>\n<td>240\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Quarterfinalist\n</th>\n<td>360</td>\n<td>430\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Semifinalist\n</th>\n<td>720</td>\n<td>780\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Runner-up\n</th>\n<td>1200</td>\n<td>1300\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Champion\n</th>\n<td>2000</td>\n<td>2000\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions">Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_champions">Past champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Past champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_gentlemen%27s_singles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon gentlemen&#39;s singles champions">Gentlemen\'s Singles</a><sup id="cite_ref-lastbritishmale_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lastbritishmale-104">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_ladies%27_singles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon ladies&#39; singles champions">Ladies\' Singles</a><sup id="cite_ref-lastbritishfemale_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lastbritishfemale-105">&#91;k&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_gentlemen%27s_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon gentlemen&#39;s doubles champions">Gentlemen\'s Doubles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_ladies%27_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon ladies&#39; doubles champions">Ladies\' Doubles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Wimbledon_mixed_doubles_champions" title="List of Wimbledon mixed doubles champions">Mixed Doubles</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_champions">Current champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Current champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg/78px-Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="78" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg/118px-Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg/157px-Novak_Djokovic_Hopman_Cup_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1206" data-file-height="1842" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Novak_Djokovic" title="Novak Djokovic">Novak Djokovic</a></b> was the winner of the Gentlemen\'s Singles in 2018. It was his thirteenth Grand Slam Men\'s Singles title and his fourth Wimbledon title.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg/76px-Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg" width="76" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg/114px-Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg/152px-Angelique_Kerber_Fed_Cup_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2428" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Angelique_Kerber" title="Angelique Kerber">Angelique Kerber</a></b> was the winner of the Ladies\' Singles in 2018. It was her third Grand Slam Women\'s Singles title and her first title at Wimbledon after previously having reached the final in 2016.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bryan_M._RG15_(5)_(19308252635).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg/80px-Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg" width="80" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg/120px-Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg/160px-Bryan_M._RG15_%285%29_%2819308252635%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2296" data-file-height="3432" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Mike_Bryan" title="Mike Bryan">Mike Bryan</a></b> was part of the winning Men\'s Doubles team in 2018. It was his seventeenth Grand Slam Men\'s Doubles title.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sock_WM14_(3)_(14643508975).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg/82px-Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg" width="82" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg/123px-Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg/163px-Sock_WM14_%283%29_%2814643508975%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2056" data-file-height="3016" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Jack_Sock" title="Jack Sock">Jack Sock</a></b> was part of the winning Men\'s Doubles team in 2018. It was his second Grand Slam Men\'s Doubles title.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krejcikova_US16_(10)_(29780173921).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg/80px-Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg" width="80" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg/121px-Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg/161px-Krejcikova_US16_%2810%29_%2829780173921%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2105" data-file-height="3139" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Barbora_Krej%C4%8D%C3%ADkov%C3%A1" title="Barbora Krej\xc4\x8d\xc3\xadkov\xc3\xa1">Barbora Krej\xc4\x8d\xc3\xadkov\xc3\xa1</a></b> was part of the winning Women\'s Doubles title in 2018. This was her second Grand Slam Women\'s Doubles title.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siniakova_BM16_(2)_(27772835415).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg/80px-Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg" width="80" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg/120px-Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg/160px-Siniakova_BM16_%282%29_%2827772835415%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="2640" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Kate%C5%99ina_Siniakov%C3%A1" title="Kate\xc5\x99ina Siniakov\xc3\xa1">Kate\xc5\x99ina Siniakov\xc3\xa1</a></b> was part of the winning Women\'s Doubles title in 2018. href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-roof-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-roof_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Except <a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a> during rain.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-draw-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-draw_3-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This means that, in the men\'s main draws, there are 128 singles (S) and 64 doubles (D), and there are 128 and 16 entrants in the respective qualifying (Q) draws.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-centrecourt-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-centrecourt_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A Centre Court did not yet exist during the first four years of the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-little_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-little-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-monday_final-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-monday_final_20-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">To date only four finals were played on a Monday due to rain: <a href="/wiki/1919_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1919 Wimbledon Championships">1919</a>, <a href="/wiki/1922_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1922 Wimbledon Championships">1922</a>, <a href="/wiki/1988_Wimbledon_Championships" title="1988 Wimbledon Championships">1988</a> and <a href="/wiki/2001_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2001 Wimbledon Championships">2001</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-gentlemen_invitation_doubles-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gentlemen_invitation_doubles_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The men who are eligible for the Gentlemen\'s Invitation Doubles are 35 years old and older.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-senior_gentlemen_invitation_doubles-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-senior_gentlemen_invitation_doubles_25-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The men who are eligible for the Senior Gentlemen\'s Invitation Doubles are 45 years old and older.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-single_elimination-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-single_elimination_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a single-elimination tournament, a losing player or team is eliminated from the tournament.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-clothing_guidelines-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-clothing_guidelines_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Guidelines regarding the prominently-white clothing rule include no solid mass of colouring; coloured trims not to exceed 1&#160;cm; shirt or dress backs to be totally white; all other items of clothing, including shorts, shirts, caps, headbands, socks, and shoe uppers to be predominantly white.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-bbccoverage-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-bbccoverage_78-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the first year of television coverage in 1937 the BBC used two cameras at the Centre Court to transmit matches for a maximum of half an hour a day. The first match to be broadcast was between <a href="/wiki/Bunny_Austin" title="Bunny Austin">Bunny Austin</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Lyttleton-Rogers" title="George Lyttleton-Rogers">George Lyttleton-Rogers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-little2013_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-little2013-77">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-lastbritishmale-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-lastbritishmale_104-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Last British Gentlemen\'s Singles champion: <a href="/wiki/Andy_Murray" title="Andy Murray">Andy Murray</a> (2016).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-lastbritishfemale-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-lastbritishfemale_105-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Last British Ladies\' Singles champion: <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Wade" title="Virginia Wade">Virginia Wade</a> (1977).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-renshaw-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-renshaw_106-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Renshaw\'s era, the defending champion was exempt from playing in the main draw, playing only in the final. This policy was abolished in 1922.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Championships,_Wimbledon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wimbledon.com/en_GB/aboutwimbledon/prize_money_and_finance.html">"Prize Money and Finance"</a>.
